    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer1993894428027714589">The acclaimed author of the cult classics <em>Trainspotting</em> and <em>The Acid House</em>, Irvine Welsh has been hailed as "the best thing that has happened to British writing in a decade" (London <em>Sunday Times</em>). This audacious novel is a brilliant (and literal) head trip of a book that brings us into the wildly active, albeit coma-beset, mind of Roy Strang, whose hallucinatory quest to e</span>
  <span id="freeText1993894428027714589" style="display:none">The acclaimed author of the cult classics <em>Trainspotting</em> and <em>The Acid House</em>, Irvine Welsh has been hailed as "the best thing that has happened to British writing in a decade" (London <em>Sunday Times</em>). This audacious novel is a brilliant (and literal) head trip of a book that brings us into the wildly active, albeit coma-beset, mind of Roy Strang, whose hallucinatory quest to eradicate the evil predator/scavenger marabou stork keeps being interrupted by grisly memories of the social and family dysfunction that brought him to this state. It is the sort of lethally funny cocktail of pathos, violence, and outrageous hilarity that only Irvine Welsh can pull off.</span>

<div id="review_1134924656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134924656" />
    <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls"><img alt="MJ Nicholls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374341850p2/2386804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134924656?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MJ Nicholls" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls">MJ Nicholls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780224036863" href="/book/show/826350.Marabou_Stork_Nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=hoots-mon">hoots-mon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134924656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11653848358107936984">Irvine Welsh was the literary hero among my generation of working-class Central Belt Scots for his graphic novels set in Edinburgh sink estates, riddled with sex, drugs, violence, and written in dextrously rendered phonetic dialect. I avoided reading Welsh, since a witless moron at my school rated <i>Trainspotting</i> his favourite book, and thereafter I associated him readers who would read his books to laugh at the banter of the characters, misunderstanding Welsh’s more sober intentions to expose the</span>
  <span id="freeText11653848358107936984" style="display:none">Irvine Welsh was the literary hero among my generation of working-class Central Belt Scots for his graphic novels set in Edinburgh sink estates, riddled with sex, drugs, violence, and written in dextrously rendered phonetic dialect. I avoided reading Welsh, since a witless moron at my school rated <i>Trainspotting</i> his favourite book, and thereafter I associated him readers who would read his books to laugh at the banter of the characters, misunderstanding Welsh’s more sober intentions to expose the shocking lives of fear and misery at the heart of places like the scheme in this novel, revelling instead in the casual hedonism aspect. Plus, I have never felt Scottish enough for Scots-centric books to speak to me. This, Welsh’s overlooked second novel, is an interesting experiment in the old coma-patient narrative, weaving a surreal/metaphorical tale of African Marabou stork-hunting around the protagonist Roy Strang’s upbringing in Edinburgh and South Africa, and his adult life as a football thug. A devastating gang rape forms the moral kernel of the novel and Welsh excels in particular in the scenes of tense horror and violence, and is less successful with the surreal humour. Smaller font size and various typographical quirks are employed to reasonable effect (with nods to Hubert Selby), although the overall product is somewhat muddled in its response to the rape (pushing into didactic repentance towards the novel’s faux-shocking over-the-top finale).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11653848358107936984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25033538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25033538" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1255581-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390288987p2/1255581.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25033538?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1255581-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25033538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7135266618098527528">I realize I haven't read Trainspotting, or even a great deal of Irvine Welsh's work, but let me go out on a limb here and say that this is my favorite.<br/><br/>The characters, especially the main character, are all deliciously real. Characteristic of Welsh, in my experience, is the atmosphere of darkness and desperation interjected with some even blacker humor. His ability to get me to sympathize with the main character, even after I'd read the end, was pretty remarkable. And not in the way you like Alex</span>
  <span id="freeText7135266618098527528" style="display:none">I realize I haven't read Trainspotting, or even a great deal of Irvine Welsh's work, but let me go out on a limb here and say that this is my favorite.<br /><br />The characters, especially the main character, are all deliciously real. Characteristic of Welsh, in my experience, is the atmosphere of darkness and desperation interjected with some even blacker humor. His ability to get me to sympathize with the main character, even after I'd read the end, was pretty remarkable. And not in the way you like Alex from A Clockwork Orange BECAUSE he's evil.<br /><br />And the nightmares, well...I won't say the nightmares are the best part because that would be misleading and also advocates a simplistic relationship with this book. But they are fantastic. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7135266618098527528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_518402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/518402" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42508-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368721201p2/42508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/518402?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/42508-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8281474098748934019">Stylistically this is Welsh's best work. Along with <i>Glue</i> it's the books of his that show him to be a really great writer who has much more up his sleeve than just drugs and violence (although he writes about these things so well, that it's not a bad thing when I say that). Why this book isn't one of those books people come in to the store looking for all the time is beyond me. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35523484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14957598315667132715">In many ways, this book was brilliant: the structure of flitting between his coma state, memories of his childhood, and an African hunting fantasy. Also, the way he physically structures words on the page really conveys the polyphonic stream of consciousness of a person in a coma. And the Scottish phonetic spellings are just plain fun. That said, this book disturbed me as no other book has done--and not in a good way. I genuinely feel traumatized by it. It is not so much the fact that violent th</span>
  <span id="freeText14957598315667132715" style="display:none">In many ways, this book was brilliant: the structure of flitting between his coma state, memories of his childhood, and an African hunting fantasy. Also, the way he physically structures words on the page really conveys the polyphonic stream of consciousness of a person in a coma. And the Scottish phonetic spellings are just plain fun. That said, this book disturbed me as no other book has done--and not in a good way. I genuinely feel traumatized by it. It is not so much the fact that violent things happen (I mean, that is life for some folks) but that it is almost naturalized through the narrative voice which so consistently embodies an incredibly hateful misogyny, homophobia, racism, etc. I mean, sometimes you can't even come up for air, and women are never referred to in anything approaching a humanizing way, always instead as crass sexual objects. Rape, torture, incest, animal torture, sexual abuse, physical abuse, meaningless sex--it's all in here. Lovely.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6618706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8911068216336466989">Harsh, inventive, horrifying, and desperately sad. Lacks the glorious sprawl of <i>Trainspotting</i>, which directly preceded it, opting instead for what may be Welsh's most tightly-coiled plotting to date. And his greatest sense of conscience, his strongest turn as a social reformer. The ending, through an appropriate scrim of sensationalism, actually manages to be both heart-rending and insightful, in a manner that Welsh rarely manages.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_386279537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386279537" />
    <a title="Ciarán West" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9012856-ciar-n-west"><img alt="Ciarán West" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490875114p2/9012856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/386279537?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ciarán West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ciarán West" href="/user/show/9012856-ciar-n-west">Ciarán West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer386279537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11129523956039258421">I think my own books are probably mostly influenced by King and Koontz (in a non-horror way), but if ever I need to justify the dialect (in Boys of Summer) or the graphic nature (in Girl Afraid), I turn to Irvine or to Chuck. When people say 'Oh, readers will find it hard to understand what your characters are saying', I point at Trainspotting, Filth, or this one, and go 'NUH-HUH!'. <br/><br/>The people have a point, of course. Not everyone can read an Irvine Welsh book. But there is a sense of smug satis</span>
  <span id="freeText11129523956039258421" style="display:none">I think my own books are probably mostly influenced by King and Koontz (in a non-horror way), but if ever I need to justify the dialect (in Boys of Summer) or the graphic nature (in Girl Afraid), I turn to Irvine or to Chuck. When people say 'Oh, readers will find it hard to understand what your characters are saying', I point at Trainspotting, Filth, or this one, and go 'NUH-HUH!'. <br /><br />The people have a point, of course. Not everyone can read an Irvine Welsh book. But there is a sense of smug satisfaction if you can, and happen to Not Be Scottish into the bargain.<br /><br />This book is in Scottish. And it's fucking horrific. I was taken to school by this novel, in terms of how depraved and vomit-inducing a book can be in its descriptions, and in the general thoughts and behaviour of its characters. And I liked it. Don't get me wrong, there is nothing wrong with an author like Alice Sebold, who can tell you a horrific tale, without giving you the gory details. In fact, like swearing in stand-up comedy, there is a skill and an art to making the reader uncomfortable without showing them the pus and the bile upfront. Equally though, there is a skill in being able to show it all, and not come off reading like a hack.<br /><br />Some of the worst self-published books out there are a product of No Editor, No Regulation, and, as well as the awful prose, their biggest flaws often involve an inability to tone down the unpalatable. In Girl Afraid, I toned down pretty much everything, but the horror still exists in the reader's mind. That alone might make them not want to carry on reading. I get that, but it's a chance I have to take.<br /><br />In this book, Welsh gives a unique viewpoint and narrative, the like of which I hadn't seen before, or haven't seen since. The story is told backwards, and there is a creeping sensation that the narrator's recollection of events might be opinion-based rather than fact. It's gripping, all the way through; and, like any of his books, the lack of a sympathetic protagonist stops being an issue once you are ensconced in the tale. You find yourself identifying with people regardless. It's a skill Welsh has, and I envy it.<br /><br />Will you like this book? It depends. Did you like any of his others? Do you have a strong stomach? Do you like to be put through an emotional wringer? Yes, yes, and yes? Then you'll love it. And you'll probably love my books too. Go read the sample of them on here, because Irvine Welsh already has enough money, and I need new Hush Puppies.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11129523956039258421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2994367114?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2994367114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9930238512038908370">This is probably one of the most horrific books I have ever read in my entire life. The list of what wasn't in this book would probably be shorter than what was in this book.<br/><br/>TW: death, gore, animal abuse, graphic animal death, rape (child and gang), violence, torture, drugs, racism, sexism etc<br/><br/><b>Marabou Stork Nightmares</b> is written by the author who wrote Trainspotting, which in itself is a wild trip - this one was like you went on an extended vacation to the bowels of hell. The blurb of the book sa</span>
  <span id="freeText9930238512038908370" style="display:none">This is probably one of the most horrific books I have ever read in my entire life. The list of what wasn't in this book would probably be shorter than what was in this book.<br /><br />TW: death, gore, animal abuse, graphic animal death, rape (child and gang), violence, torture, drugs, racism, sexism etc<br /><br /><b>Marabou Stork Nightmares</b> is written by the author who wrote Trainspotting, which in itself is a wild trip - this one was like you went on an extended vacation to the bowels of hell. The blurb of the book says <i> It is the sort of lethally funny cocktail of pathos, violence, and outrageous hilarity that only Irvine Welsh can pull off.</i>, I don't know where they got the funny part from because there wasn't a single part of this book that I would even nose exhale at.<br /><br />I am genuinely disturbed by some of the stuff written in this book - I had to take a breather and then there was some that I just had to skip because I couldn't handle it (namely: Winston Two). I don't think I would ever recommend this book to anyone. I have never read a MC that I have disliked more - though I can understand that violence begets violence, but it's not an excuse.<br /><br />I can appreciate the literary style that Welsh was going for with this book, that was quite interesting and I liked the way the typography appeared throughout the book - it was quite new, to me, and something I haven't really seen before. The switches from going the nightmares, memories and current time was incredibly well done and I was able to follow whereabouts we were timeline-wise. Unfortunately that's the only part of the book that I can appreciate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9930238512038908370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130288035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10804884604851440654">Mind. Blown.<br/><br/>The angle of this story is incredible to begin with; a coma patient tell his story.<br/><br/>Sometimes, he (Roy) slipps close to the surface and hears conversations or music around him, a level below that he recounts actual memories from his life, and even deeper, he hunts the metaphorical stork with his friend and companion, footballer Sandy Jameison. He feels that he will be ready to resurface and wake up when he finally kills the stork, which he believes encompasses everything negative and </span>
  <span id="freeText10804884604851440654" style="display:none">Mind. Blown.<br /><br />The angle of this story is incredible to begin with; a coma patient tell his story.<br /><br />Sometimes, he (Roy) slipps close to the surface and hears conversations or music around him, a level below that he recounts actual memories from his life, and even deeper, he hunts the metaphorical stork with his friend and companion, footballer Sandy Jameison. He feels that he will be ready to resurface and wake up when he finally kills the stork, which he believes encompasses everything negative and harmful that he's experienced in his life. <br /><br />A lot of what Roy recounts from his childhood is sad and pathetic, while much of his adulthood memories are disgusting and violent. Many different mature themes are discussed, such as the drinking of alcohol, taking of illegal drugs, physical violence, rape... this is not a book for the faint of heart.<br /><br />When I finished it, I just sort of sat there, staring blankly ahead of me, my mind racing with what had just been revealed. It's that sort of book.<br /><br />If you're not afraid of violent cursing as well as the aforementioned themes, then go ahead and read this fantastic book. Modern Scottish literature at its finest...<br /><br />Very. Good. Stuff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10804884604851440654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2635510187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2635510187" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55933142-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510508138p2/55933142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2635510187?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/55933142-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55933142-angela?shelf=summer-challenge2019">summer-challenge2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55933142-angela?shelf=ron-picks">ron-picks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2635510187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14656048899963301768">Summer Reading Challenge 4/27<br/><br/>Continental Drift [1/7: Europe] - “Read a book set on every continent”<br/><br/>This might be the toughest book I’ve had to write a review for. How do you rate a book that had a compelling story, from a culture and writer you have a connection to, but with a writing style that made it very difficult for me to read?<br/><br/>I first picked up Marabou Stork Nightmares (MSN) back in December. I immediately missed the main concept of the book, which is that the main character is in a coma -</span>
  <span id="freeText14656048899963301768" style="display:none">Summer Reading Challenge 4/27<br /><br />Continental Drift [1/7: Europe] - “Read a book set on every continent”<br /><br />This might be the toughest book I’ve had to write a review for. How do you rate a book that had a compelling story, from a culture and writer you have a connection to, but with a writing style that made it very difficult for me to read?<br /><br />I first picked up Marabou Stork Nightmares (MSN) back in December. I immediately missed the main concept of the book, which is that the main character is in a coma - so I wasn’t off to a great start. After realizing that I would have to read carefully and interpret around a lack of clear timeline shifts and basic grammar, I started the book over again. Three times. <br /><br />I have never been great at following surreal, stream-of-conscious type stories. This one really tested my reading comprehension, but in the end it was so worth it. <br /><br />The aggressive and diverse language, which was originally very off putting to me, was actually key to creating an uncomfortable atmosphere. Nothing about this novel was feel-good or cheerful, but it was an effective gut punch that I haven't been able to stop thinking about.<br /><br />I am reluctant to give away much of the story, as to talk too much about the main character Roy Strang would risk mitigating the impact going on his journey may have on you. <br /><br />Reading Irvine Welsh was not easy for me, even though I absolutely adore Scotland and was looking forward to enjoying this celebrated Scottish author. He has definitely depicted a brutal and hopeless world, and my understanding is his other novels are no different. I am determined to pick up another, and now that I am more familiar with Welsh, the dialect (Scottish slang) he uses, and the brutal worlds he creates, I am hoping I will get pulled in quicker with the next one.<br /><br />If you like experimental (“different”) writing styles, I would ignore how much trouble I had getting drawn into the story, and I encourage you to pick up MSN. The hunt for the Marabou Stork will leave you guessing who is predator and who is prey?</span>
  <a data-text-id="14656048899963301768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16477472770788653997">This book left me freaked out for weeks. It's told from the perspective of someone in a coma, drifting in and out of three levels of awareness: nearly aware of his real surroundings; remembering the events of his life that led him to be in this coma; and in a surreal fantasy African safari. Very well written, easy to follow despite the narrative tricks, and with a narrator that will draw you in somewhat against your will. </span>

        <a title="Ellie Spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie Spencer" href="/user/show/93944772-ellie-spencer">Ellie Spencer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3504359580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18141064761327861772">Wow. I really enjoyed trainspotting, but this book was on another level. I think it’s going to take me a while to fully process what I have read.<br/><br/>Marabou stork nightmares follows Roy Strang who is in a coma. We see the fantasy world he has created, the memories of his past that slowly creep back and the discussions he can hear happing around his hospital bed.<br/><br/>This book was a truly harrowing read. It was intensely dark and difficult to read at times (because of the topic nature). But I simply did n</span>
  <span id="freeText18141064761327861772" style="display:none">Wow. I really enjoyed trainspotting, but this book was on another level. I think it’s going to take me a while to fully process what I have read.<br /><br />Marabou stork nightmares follows Roy Strang who is in a coma. We see the fantasy world he has created, the memories of his past that slowly creep back and the discussions he can hear happing around his hospital bed.<br /><br />This book was a truly harrowing read. It was intensely dark and difficult to read at times (because of the topic nature). But I simply did not want to put it down! I loved how unique the writing was. It took me a little while to get used to the writing and what it conveyed, but once I did, it flowed seamlessly. <br /><br />Roy Strang is a character that I simultaneously despise and feel a great sympathy for. Welsh created a life for him that seemed so real. <br /><br />I would definitely recommend this book, but only with the warning that some topics may be triggering for some! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18141064761327861772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2422640356?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.M. Hushour" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour">J.M. Hushour</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780393038453" href="/book/show/826349.Marabou_Stork_Nightmares">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422640356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3458056017788616644">"Humans are into animals whose qualities they covet, and hate ones whose characteristics they vainly like to feel are not at all 'human'. The world we live in is not run by cuddly, strong bears, graceful sleek cats or loyal, friendly dogs. Marabou Storks run this place, and they are known as nasty bastards."<br/><br/>Roy Strang, coma patient, casually cashie, and half-hearted psychopath divides his time in-coma between fuddling over his shitty, shitty life and hunting the dreaded title bird in homoerotic </span>
  <span id="freeText3458056017788616644" style="display:none">"Humans are into animals whose qualities they covet, and hate ones whose characteristics they vainly like to feel are not at all 'human'. The world we live in is not run by cuddly, strong bears, graceful sleek cats or loyal, friendly dogs. Marabou Storks run this place, and they are known as nasty bastards."<br /><br />Roy Strang, coma patient, casually cashie, and half-hearted psychopath divides his time in-coma between fuddling over his shitty, shitty life and hunting the dreaded title bird in homoerotic Africa. Welsh ups his game with this hilarious and, let's be frank, extremely disturbing novel. The structure is fun and playful, as the very-aware Strang battles against what he can hear from the real world outside him by delving deeper into his hunt for the Stork.<br />Probably not for the faint-hearted or easily-offended, but a ballsy harrowing into one radge's hell.</span>

<div id="review_2373892631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373892631" />
    <a title="Guy Portman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11566536-guy-portman"><img alt="Guy Portman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539458477p2/11566536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2373892631?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Guy Portman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Guy Portman" href="/user/show/11566536-guy-portman">Guy Portman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11566536-guy-portman?shelf=transgressive">transgressive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2373892631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6284307266889643019">3.5 *<br/><br/>Roy Strang narrates this story from the hospital in which he is lying in a coma. It begins in South Africa, where he and his friend Sandy Jamieson are hunting the environmental havoc-wreaking, scavenger/predator marabou stork. The account soon shifts to Roy’s working-class upbringing in Scotland and South Africa; an upbringing marred by a dysfunctional family and abuse. We follow Roy through to early adulthood. Along the way are escapades, brutality, bullying, girls, drinking, bird watching</span>
  <span id="freeText6284307266889643019" style="display:none">3.5 *<br /><br />Roy Strang narrates this story from the hospital in which he is lying in a coma. It begins in South Africa, where he and his friend Sandy Jamieson are hunting the environmental havoc-wreaking, scavenger/predator marabou stork. The account soon shifts to Roy’s working-class upbringing in Scotland and South Africa; an upbringing marred by a dysfunctional family and abuse. We follow Roy through to early adulthood. Along the way are escapades, brutality, bullying, girls, drinking, bird watching, ‘fitba’ violence and a horrific crime that will have far-reaching ramifications.<br /><br />This is an inventive book, boasting parallel stories and different levels of awareness. It is peppered with stylistic idiosyncrasies. These include the utilisation in places of a smaller font size, as well as passages in which the text is presented diagonally.<br /><br />The early chapters of this bleak and at times harrowing work are eminently readable. However, the story loses direction somewhat and there is a lot of glossing over in the latter stages. Marabou Stork Nightmares is far from Irvine Welsh’s best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6284307266889643019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126965968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126965968" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4395669-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287540158p2/4395669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126965968?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4395669-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126965968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17290620064439845991">My first time through this book I thought Irvine Welsh had completely reinvented himself. The beginning of the novel left me thinking that the entirety was going to be some deranged acid trip of whirring images and slurred sounds. It doesn't take long for Welsh to slip into his familiar role of Edinburgh scheme documentarian, a role of which he is the master.<br/><br/>The reader travels between Roy Strang's African dreamland and his memory of growing up in the toughest part of Edinburgh. Gradually, you re</span>
  <span id="freeText17290620064439845991" style="display:none">My first time through this book I thought Irvine Welsh had completely reinvented himself. The beginning of the novel left me thinking that the entirety was going to be some deranged acid trip of whirring images and slurred sounds. It doesn't take long for Welsh to slip into his familiar role of Edinburgh scheme documentarian, a role of which he is the master.<br /><br />The reader travels between Roy Strang's African dreamland and his memory of growing up in the toughest part of Edinburgh. Gradually, you realize that the African element of the novel is the least important to informing the characters in this book. Through the scheme flashbacks the reader comes to sympathize with Roy despite his less than stellar moral fiber. In Roy Strang Welsh has built up a character so strong that you almost (ALMOST) feel sorry for what happens to him in the end.<br /><br />This novel gets slagged because it apparently doesn't live up to Trainspotting, but Welsh has taken the best parts of that novel (the character development, the scheme imagery, etc.) and applied to one central character. At times you almost forget that Roy lies comatose in a hospital, but you will remember the images Welsh puts into your mind. Do yourself a favor and read this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17290620064439845991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_189886509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189886509" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2744544-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465764198p2/2744544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/189886509?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/2744544-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/14320695-marabou-stork-nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189886509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10862672902026437800"><br/>Irvine Welsh's second novel is probably his best one, even better than Trainspotting. The story consists of Roy Strang, an oddball who's obsessed with birds, with the exception of Marabou Storks and invade his dreams.<br/><br/>As Roy is growing up he encounters the usual trials, bullying, going out with girls, doing drugs etc. However his problems start when he devises a brutal form of revenge on the snobbiest girl at school. <br/><br/>Early Welsh could do no wrong and with this book the scene shifts from the prese</span>
  <span id="freeText10862672902026437800" style="display:none"><br />Irvine Welsh's second novel is probably his best one, even better than Trainspotting. The story consists of Roy Strang, an oddball who's obsessed with birds, with the exception of Marabou Storks and invade his dreams.<br /><br />As Roy is growing up he encounters the usual trials, bullying, going out with girls, doing drugs etc. However his problems start when he devises a brutal form of revenge on the snobbiest girl at school. <br /><br />Early Welsh could do no wrong and with this book the scene shifts from the present day, Roy's disturbing past (spoiler: a dog dies a brutal death) and a meta-narrative of Roy hunting a stork in South Africa. Soon all narratives get mixed up and Roy cannot distinguish between his fantasy world and the cruel reality and life changing actions he is performing. <br /><br />Marabou Stork Nightmares display Welsh's themes at their best: Violence, Social commentary and Drugs. There's a feminist slant to this novel, which I liked as well. Definitely the best one to start with if you've never read Welsh before. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10862672902026437800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10479366679139731090">Irvine Welsh is sometimes hard for me to read; his characters are the kind of people you know exist in the world, but you wish they didn't. There are no heroes (well, sometimes there's an antihero), and the protagonist is usually the character you come to hate the most. That being said, however, his books are always powerful, always disturbing, and always very well written. If you can't handle gratuitous violence, these are not the books for you. If you sometimes like a book that makes you want </span>
  <span id="freeText10479366679139731090" style="display:none">Irvine Welsh is sometimes hard for me to read; his characters are the kind of people you know exist in the world, but you wish they didn't. There are no heroes (well, sometimes there's an antihero), and the protagonist is usually the character you come to hate the most. That being said, however, his books are always powerful, always disturbing, and always very well written. If you can't handle gratuitous violence, these are not the books for you. If you sometimes like a book that makes you want to scream and laugh at the same time, you might like these. I still haven't read Trainspotting, although I enjoyed the movie... maybe I'll get up the nerve sometime.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer791899179821491752">This book was incredibly disturbing- I literally felt sick to my stomach reading some parts- but that is clearly Welsh's intent and he does it through innovative typography and storytelling. Marabou Stork Nightmares tackles misogyny, sexism, pedophilia, rape, and so many other things but it's truly thought-provoking and I would definitely read Welsh's other books. </span>

<div id="review_1667271157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1667271157" />
    <a title="Dane Cobain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19638210-dane-cobain"><img alt="Dane Cobain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571333550p2/19638210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1667271157?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dane Cobain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dane Cobain" href="/user/show/19638210-dane-cobain">Dane Cobain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1667271157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16923032629945493339">This book was probably my favourite of all of the Irvine Welsh books that I’ve read so far, although I do still have three or four to work through. And there’s a big twist at the end of it that I’m going to have to try to avoid spoiling, but it knocked me for six and left a lasting memory, so much so that whilst I haven’t re-read it yet, I want to.<br/><br/>It features Welsh’s inimitable writing style, as his work always does, but it also plays with elements like the layout of the book, and spacing, and i</span>
  <span id="freeText16923032629945493339" style="display:none">This book was probably my favourite of all of the Irvine Welsh books that I’ve read so far, although I do still have three or four to work through. And there’s a big twist at the end of it that I’m going to have to try to avoid spoiling, but it knocked me for six and left a lasting memory, so much so that whilst I haven’t re-read it yet, I want to.<br /><br />It features Welsh’s inimitable writing style, as his work always does, but it also plays with elements like the layout of the book, and spacing, and it just generally qualifies as some of the author’s more experimental work. Considering that he’s already ‘alternative‘, and well away from what most people think of as a mainstream writer, you can see why that means this might be difficult to read, although it’s worth soldiering on and it’s not too different from some of the other experimental stuff that I’ve seen, but then I seek it out.<br /><br />This is a pretty good book to start out with if you’re new to Welsh’s work, but I wouldn’t say that it’s exactly representative – it’s just different, and that’s what makes it worth recommending. Welsh has written plenty of good books, and all of them are worth reading, but this stands out from them by being different and so it’s definitely earned a place on your bookcase. So what are you waiting for? Go out and grab a copy of it so you can read it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16923032629945493339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1247346937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247346937" />
    <a title="Martin Boyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20229798-martin-boyle"><img alt="Martin Boyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368216252p2/20229798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247346937?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martin Boyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martin Boyle" href="/user/show/20229798-martin-boyle">Martin Boyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 978009943511" href="/book/show/9658725-marabou-stork-nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20229798-martin-boyle?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247346937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882662812566629211">This is a deeply unpleasant story. There is nothing to like about Roy Strang or his family, or his friends, or his world of mindless and casual violence.<br/><br/>But as Roy's story forces its way through the grotesque nightmares - themselves repulsive - based around a hatred of the marabou stork, you realise that the nightmares are a shield against the unpleasantness of his current predicament and his even worse and more frightening memories. Memories that led to desperation even in someone as callous as</span>
  <span id="freeText17882662812566629211" style="display:none">This is a deeply unpleasant story. There is nothing to like about Roy Strang or his family, or his friends, or his world of mindless and casual violence.<br /><br />But as Roy's story forces its way through the grotesque nightmares - themselves repulsive - based around a hatred of the marabou stork, you realise that the nightmares are a shield against the unpleasantness of his current predicament and his even worse and more frightening memories. Memories that led to desperation even in someone as callous as Roy.<br /><br />I guess the reputation of Irvine Welsh should have warned me!<br /><br />The book is imaginatively told in its unsettling typesetting and in the erratic way the story unfolds. Prepare for sharp changes of scene, sudden recalibrations of expectation or perspective (never for the better!). Even the storks retain a power to surprise.<br /><br />Don't read this without due warning. And don't believe the critics' suggestions that it is "a funny ... novel. But it is a strong novel and gives an unsettling glimpse of a world I'd rather not be too acquainted with: this is as close as I want to get!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17882662812566629211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_651948420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/651948420" />
    <a title="Kalin Rheanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21680052-kalin-rheanne"><img alt="Kalin Rheanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372283323p2/21680052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/651948420?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kalin Rheanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kalin Rheanne" href="/user/show/21680052-kalin-rheanne">Kalin Rheanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651948420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6852550336729913073">A masterpiece of style and characterization, Maribou Stork Nightmares is rife with poignant themes which are extremely relevant today, and perhaps will always be. Welsh has simultaneously written in a way that is blatant with its symbolism, but layered to make the text enjoyable and accessible to readers of all levels. The phonetic spelling of the Scottish accent sprinkled throughout is tough to discern at first but reading comes with ease after a chapter or two, so I highly recommend pushing th</span>
  <span id="freeText6852550336729913073" style="display:none">A masterpiece of style and characterization, Maribou Stork Nightmares is rife with poignant themes which are extremely relevant today, and perhaps will always be. Welsh has simultaneously written in a way that is blatant with its symbolism, but layered to make the text enjoyable and accessible to readers of all levels. The phonetic spelling of the Scottish accent sprinkled throughout is tough to discern at first but reading comes with ease after a chapter or two, so I highly recommend pushing through.<br /><br />Roy is a complex character to say the least. Welsh has developed three distinct yet interwoven persona for the man. The reader is force to empathize with and understand Roy while simultaneously jerked through his split mind and experiences, including his own gut wrenching acts, which challenges concepts of morality and humanity.<br /><br />A nightmare in itself, reflecting the most savage aspects of humanity, Maribou Stork Nightmares is a must read. And despite its advanced philosophical, political, social, and psychological themes, Nightmares is deliciously entertaining and hilarious (for those with a dark sense of humor).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6852550336729913073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_550163627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/550163627" />
    <a title="Vicky Parkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17968528-vicky-parkinson"><img alt="Vicky Parkinson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550163627?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicky Parkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicky Parkinson" href="/user/show/17968528-vicky-parkinson">Vicky Parkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/14320695-marabou-stork-nightmares">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550163627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8534430581468869655">Its a difficult book to explain without giving the game away too much or making it sound a bit more superficial than I think it actually is.<br/><br/>So, we have an instantly dislikeable narrator who is telling his story from a hospital bed whilst in a coma. He's flitting between levels of consciousness, seemingly at will, to avoid what's going on around him but also to avoid the depths of his psyche which takes the form of an African adventure in search of the Marabou Stork. Yep. Not what I was expecting</span>
  <span id="freeText8534430581468869655" style="display:none">Its a difficult book to explain without giving the game away too much or making it sound a bit more superficial than I think it actually is.<br /><br />So, we have an instantly dislikeable narrator who is telling his story from a hospital bed whilst in a coma. He's flitting between levels of consciousness, seemingly at will, to avoid what's going on around him but also to avoid the depths of his psyche which takes the form of an African adventure in search of the Marabou Stork. Yep. Not what I was expecting either.<br /><br />It's an engrossing exploration of the cycle of abuse and poverty among many other socio-economic issues, placed in a narrative which we can never quite trust. Blame is also an interesting theme here. Are people who do bad things simply making a choice to be evil or is there more to it than that in which case who's fault is it?<br /><br />I liked it. I'm not a huge fan of other Irvine Welsh novels so if like me, you'd given up on Porno and Trainspotting, don't give up on Irvine Welsh altogether and give this one a go.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8534430581468869655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('erSqTVeeTDa6zCV/qVzfq/iLS+Q2W99R7RJayfOSTSQaRQN1izgJqML0eyeyeWzuw0kbq7pX02RuEd1nbNvoGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6vB1S+tqv4JZqwmFH9D3iHM9XFG48f+lgXURD3CW2ViKAdxzN8z6HCGTV90E9UTNSP8MHjT985ACdpah7998ZQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

After an evening of routine debauchery, traipsing from toilet to toilet and partaking in a host of narcotics, the middle-aged painter wakes to discover that his girlfriend, Sarah, has turned into a chimpanzee. Simon is also a chimp, but he does not accept this fact—he is convinced that he is still human.\n\nHe is then confined to an emergency psychiatric ward and placed under the care of alpha-psychiatrist Dr. Zack Busner. Dr. Zack Busner—also a medical doctor, radical psychoanalyst, maverick axiolytic drug researcher, and former television personality—is prepared to help Simon get used to &quot;chimpunity&quot;.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18358195673209862133">Probably most famous for his gritty depiction of a gang of Scottish Heroin addicts, <i>Trainspotting</i> (1993), Welsh focuses on the darker side of human nature and drug use. All of his novels are set in his native Scotland and filled with anti-heroes, small time crooks and hooligans. Welsh manages, however to imbue these characters with a sad humanity that makes them likable despite their obvious scumb</span>
  <span id="freeText18358195673209862133" style="display:none">Probably most famous for his gritty depiction of a gang of Scottish Heroin addicts, <i>Trainspotting</i> (1993), Welsh focuses on the darker side of human nature and drug use. All of his novels are set in his native Scotland and filled with anti-heroes, small time crooks and hooligans. Welsh manages, however to imbue these characters with a sad humanity that makes them likable despite their obvious scumbaggerry. Irvine Welsh is also known for writing in his native Edinburgh Scots dialect, making his prose challenging for the average reader unfamiliar with this style.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18358195673209862133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
